<p>The <b>Audi A6</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Executive_car" title="Executive car">executive car</a> made by the German <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automaker</a> <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi AG</a>, now in its fourth generation. As the successor to the <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a>, the A6 is manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Neckarsulm" title="Neckarsulm">Neckarsulm</a>, Germany – and is available in sedan and <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">wagon</a> configurations, the latter marketed by Audi as the <i>Avant.</i> Audi's internal numbering treats the A6 as a continuation of the Audi 100 lineage, with the initial A6 designated as a member of the C4-series, followed by the C5, C6, and the C7. The C7 version of the A6 is built on the Volkswagen Group MLB platform shared with many other Audi models and potentially one Porsche model within the Volkswagen Group.[3] The related <a href="/wiki/Audi_A7" title="Audi A7">Audi A7</a> is essentially a coupé-hatchback version of the C7-series A6, but is marketed under its own separate identity and model designation.</p>
<p>All generations of the A6 have offered either <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a> or <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> – marketed by Audi as their <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)"><i>quattro</i></a> system. Second- and third- generation A6 models have shared their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_platform" title="Automobile platform">platform</a> with the company's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_A6_allroad_quattro" title="Audi A6 allroad quattro">Allroad</a> models.</p>

<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Avant</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Executive_car" title="Executive car">executive car</a> was previously named the <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a> (or Audi 5000 in the United States), and was released in three successive generations (<a href="/wiki/Audi_100#C1" title="Audi 100">Audi C1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_100#C2" title="Audi 100">Audi C2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_100#C3" title="Audi 100">Audi C3</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carautoportal_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-carautoportal-2">[2]</a></sup> In 1994, the latest generation (C4) of the <a href="/wiki/Audi_100#C4" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a> received a facelift and was renamed as the <b>Audi A6</b>, to fit in with Audi's new <a href="/wiki/Alphanumeric" title="Alphanumeric">alphanumeric</a> <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature" title="Nomenclature">nomenclature</a> (as the full-size <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">A8</a> had just been introduced). The exterior was changed only slightly from the "C4" Audi 100 – new front and rear lights, new radiator <a href="/wiki/Grille" title="Grille">grille</a>, similarly with <a href="/wiki/Chassis" title="Chassis">chassis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">engine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(mechanics)" title="Transmission (mechanics)">transmission</a> choices. The United Kingdom was the first market to receive the A6, as stock of <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">RHD</a> Audi 100s had run out before expected, and before the rest of mainland Europe.</p>
<p>The new engines for the A6 were 1.8-litre <a href="/wiki/Multi-valve" title="Multi-valve">20v</a> <a href="/wiki/Inline-four_engine" title="Inline-four engine">inline four-cylinder</a>, 2.6-Litre 12V <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6</a> and 2.8-litre 30v <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engines</a>, with the 2.3-litre <a href="/wiki/Straight-five_engine" title="Straight-five engine">inline five engine</a> being dropped on most markets. For the <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a>, an inline four 1.9 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">Turbocharged Direct Injection</a> (TDI), and the inline five (R5) 2.5 TDI (103 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kW</a> (140 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 138 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>)) were available.</p>
<p>Until 1997, the A6 came with several different engines, two of them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbodiesel" title="Turbodiesel">turbodiesel</a>, and most of them available with Audi's <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> system. The A6 was available with saloon and Avant bodies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="C4_engines">C4 engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: C4 engines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S6">S6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: S6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_1997_(8808376949).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg/220px-Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg/330px-Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg/440px-Audi_S6_1997_%288808376949%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_1997_(8808376949).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi S6</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_(14477159915).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg/220px-Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg/330px-Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg/440px-Audi_S6_%2814477159915%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_(14477159915).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi S6</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon introducing the C4 series A6, Audi made small revisions to what was previously known as the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4" title="Audi S4">Audi S4</a>, renaming it the <b>Audi S6</b>; the S4 name would eventually be re-used for a completely different model derived from Audi's smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_B_platform" title="Volkswagen B platform">Volkswagen Group B platform</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a>. As this was the first S6 model from Audi, it is commonly referred to as the <i><a href="/wiki/Audi_Ur-S4_/_Ur-S6" title="Audi Ur-S4 / Ur-S6">Ur-S6</a></i>, derived from the German augmentive, "<b>Ur</b>sprünglich" (meaning: original). It was available as both a <a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">saloon/sedan</a> (<i>typ</i> 4A5), and an "Avant" (<i>typ</i> 4A9) (<a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">estate/wagon</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> customers, but only as a saloon in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.</p>
<p>From its launch in late 1994, the Audi S6 was powered by a 2,226 <a href="/wiki/Cubic_centimetre" title="Cubic centimetre">cubic centimetres</a> (135.8 <a href="/wiki/Cubic_inch" title="Cubic inch">cu in</a>) <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbocharged</a> <a href="/wiki/Straight-five_engine" title="Straight-five engine">inline five-cylinder</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engine</a> (parts code prefix: 034, identification code: AAN) with a <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a> <a href="/wiki/Motronic" title="Motronic">Motronic</a> electronic <a href="/wiki/Engine_control_unit" title="Engine control unit">engine control unit</a> (ECU), producing a <a href="/wiki/Motive_power" title="Motive power">motive</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">power</a> output of 169 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (230 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 227 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>) at 5,900 <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_per_minute" title="Revolutions per minute">revolutions per minute</a> (rpm), and 326 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (240 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>) at around 1,950 rpm, whilst consuming high <a href="/wiki/Octane_rating" title="Octane rating">octane</a> "Super Plus" 98RON unleaded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrol" title="Petrol">petrol</a>. This powerful <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">engine</a> gave the S6 good performance with a top speed of 235 kilometres per hour (146.0 mph), and 0 to 100 km/h (62.1 mph) in 6.7 <a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">seconds</a>; with 160 km/h (99.4 mph) being reached in 17.5 seconds. The vehicle was available with a standard six-speed <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">manual transmission</a> (five-speed only in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>), and Audi's dynamic <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a> T-1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quattro_(four_wheel_drive_system)" title="Quattro (four wheel drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> system.</p>
<p>Audi made a high-performance, 4.2-litre <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8 engine</a> (parts code prefix: 077, identification code: AEC) with a Bosch KE-Motronic ECU available as an option in the original <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> S4s, and made the decision to continue to do so with the S6, making a 213 kilowatts (290 PS; 286 bhp) version of the 4.2 available as an optional upgrade over the 2.2-litre inline five-cylinder turbo. Unlike the five-cylinder turbocharged version, the V8-powered S6 was supplied with a four-speed <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a> as standard, but kept the quattro four wheel drive. A six-speed manual gearbox was also available as an option.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_S6_PLUS">Audi S6 PLUS<span id="S6.2B"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Audi S6 PLUS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="408" data-file-width="721" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg/220px-Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg/330px-Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg/440px-Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S6_Plus_Limousine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi S6 Plus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Swan_song" title="Swan song">swan song</a> to the C4 platform, an even more powerful, and very limited-production <b>Audi S6 PLUS</b> was briefly available to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> customers. The S6 PLUS, developed by Audi's wholly owned high performance subsidiary, <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quattro_GmbH" title="Quattro GmbH">quattro GmbH</a></b>, was available for sale during the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Model_year" title="Model year">model year</a> only (production from June 1996 to October 1997). A total of 952 cars were produced–855 Avant, and 97 saloons.</p>
<p>It was powered by another version of the <a href="/wiki/Multi-valve" title="Multi-valve">32-valve</a> (four valves per cylinder) 4.2-litre <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8 engine</a> (parts code prefix: 077, identification code: AHK, later to be seen in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_S8" title="Audi S8">Audi S8</a> as AKH). Audi's performance division reworked key parts of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a>, increasing the <a href="/wiki/Motive_power" title="Motive power">motive</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">power</a> to 240 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (326 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 322 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>). It was only available with a revised six-speed <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">manual transmission</a> (parts code prefix: 01E, identification code: DGU) (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gear_ratio" title="Gear ratio">gear ratios</a> – 1st: 3.500, 2nd: 1.889, 3rd: 1.320, 4th: 1.034, 5th: 0.857, 6th: 0.730), with a final drive ratio of 4.111.</p>
<p>Further revisions were made to the suspension, <a href="/wiki/Brake" title="Brake">brakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">roadwheels</a>. The front <a href="/wiki/Disc_brake" title="Disc brake">brake discs</a> were enlarged to 323 millimetres (12.7 in) in diameter by 30 mm (1.18 in) thick. Standard roadwheels were 8Jx17 "Avus" cast aluminium <a href="/wiki/Alloy_wheel" title="Alloy wheel">alloy wheels</a>, with an optional 7Jx16 alloy wheel for use with winter tyres was also available.</p>
<p>With so much power on tap, the S6 Plus saloon could reach 100 kilometres per hour (62.1 mph) from a standstill in 5.6 seconds, with the Avant a tenth of a second slower at 5.7 seconds.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p><span id="C5"></span></p>

<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Engine</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 1997, the introduction of a new A6 (<b><i>Typ</i> 4B</b>), based on a new design <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_platform" title="Automobile platform">automobile platform</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group_C_platform#C5" title="Volkswagen Group C platform">Volkswagen Group C5 platform</a>, with a new range of <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engines</a> was announced and appeared in March at the 1997 Geneva Motor Show. This new A6 moved up a notch in quality, and was marketed in the same categories as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_5-Series" title="BMW 5-Series">BMW 5-Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_E-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz E-Class">Mercedes-Benz E-Class</a>. The redesigned body presented a modern design, with a fastback styling which set the trend for the Audi lineup, and gave the relatively large <a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">saloon</a> an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerodynamic" title="Aerodynamic">aerodynamic</a> shell with a low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_drag" title="Coefficient of drag">coefficient of drag</a> of 0.28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000 and 2001, the "C5" A6 was on <a href="/wiki/Car_and_Driver" title="Car and Driver">Car and Driver</a> magazine's <i>Ten Best</i> list. This new A6 was available with a wide range of engines and configurations. The <a href="/wiki/Multi-valve" title="Multi-valve">30-valve</a> 2.4- and 2.8-litre <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6 engines</a> represented the bulk of the A6's development programme, with a multitude of other engine configurations available throughout the globe. As an alternative to the <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">manual transmission</a>, a five-speed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiptronic" title="Tiptronic">tiptronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a> was also available.</p>
<p>The C5 saloon variant arrived in mid-1997 in Europe, late 1997 in North America and Australia, and the Avant in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In Canada, there was no Avant (Audi's name for an <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">estate/wagon</a>) available at all in 1998 – Audi dropped the C4 Avant at the end of the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Model_year" title="Model year">model year</a>, and jumped straight to the C5 Avant in 1998 in conjunction with its release in the US. As a result of complying with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FMVSS" title="FMVSS">FMVSS</a>, the North American models were equipped with front and rear <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bumper_(automobile)" title="Bumper (automobile)">bumpers</a> that protruded several inches further than their European counterparts, with modified brackets and bumper suspension assemblies as result, and child-seat tethers for occupant safety. In compliance with Canadian law, Canadian models received <a href="/wiki/Daytime_running_lamp" title="Daytime running lamp">daytime running lights</a> as standard equipment. North American C5 A6 models received the 2.8-litre, 30-valve V6 engine, the 2.7-litre <a href="/wiki/Twin-turbo" title="Twin-turbo">"biturbo"</a> V6 (also found in the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4#B5" title="Audi S4">B5 platform S4</a>, 250 PS (180 kW; 250 hp)), and the 4.2-litre 40-valve <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engine</a> (300 PS (220 kW; 300 hp)); the two higher-spec. engines were only offered with <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a>. The V8 models arrived with significantly altered exterior body panels, with slightly more flared <a href="/wiki/Fender_(vehicle)" title="Fender (vehicle)">wheel arches (fenders)</a>, revised <a href="/wiki/Headlamp" title="Headlamp">headlamps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grille" title="Grille">grille</a> design (before being introduced in 2002 to all other A6 models), larger <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">roadwheels</a> (8Jx17-inch), larger <a href="/wiki/Brake" title="Brake">brakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> as standard.</p>
<p>In 2002, the A6 received a facelift, with revised headlight and grille design, exposed exhaust tips, and slight changes to accessory <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Body_molding" title="Body molding">body moldings</a>, and taillight colour from red to amber in North American models. A new host of engines were also introduced. The 1.8-litre engine was deleted and replaced by a 2.0-litre powerplant with 96 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (131 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 129 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>). The 1.9-litre <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">Turbocharged Direct Injection</a> (TDI) was tweaked to produce a maximum <a href="/wiki/Motive_power" title="Motive power">motive</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">power</a> output of 96 kilowatts (131 PS; 129 bhp), and 310 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (229 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">torque</a>, receiving a six-speed <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">manual gearbox</a> in the process. The 2.4-litre V6 gained an extra 5 hp and better balancing, and the 2.8-litre V6 engine was replaced by a 3.0-litre engine with 162 kilowatts (220 PS; 217 bhp). The turbocharged 2.7-litre was revised, resulting in 184 kilowatts (250 PS; 247 bhp) and 330 newton metres (243 lbf·ft), controlled by standard quattro. The V6 diesel was also slightly modified resulting in 120 kilowatts (163 PS; 161 bhp) (after the second modification) and 350 newton metres (258 lbf·ft). A new more powerful V6 diesel was also introduced with 132 kilowatts (179 PS; 177 bhp) and 370 newton metres (273 lbf·ft). The 4.2-litre V8 engine which arrived in 2001 remained unchanged.</p>
<p>Also new was the <a href="/wiki/Multitronic" title="Multitronic">multitronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Continuously_variable_transmission" title="Continuously variable transmission">continuously variable transmission</a>, available in most <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a> models. All models, except the 2.0-litre petrol and 1.9-litre TDI, were available with Audi's trademark four-wheel-drive system, quattro. A four-wheel-drive version of the Avant, with raised ground clearance and slightly altered styling was sold as the <a href="/wiki/Audi_allroad_quattro" title="Audi allroad quattro">Audi allroad quattro</a>, Audi's first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crossover_SUV" title="Crossover SUV">crossover SUV</a>.</p>
<p>The second-generation A6 was on <i><a href="/wiki/Car_and_Driver" title="Car and Driver">Car and Driver</a></i> magazine's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Car_and_Driver_Ten_Best" title="Car and Driver Ten Best">Ten Best list</a> for 2000 and 2001. The updated 2005 A6 won the <i><a href="/wiki/World_Car_of_the_Year" title="World Car of the Year">World Car of the Year</a></i> award for 2005. In addition, the facelifted third-generation A6 3.0T won two Car and Driver "comparos" that pitted it against other sedans like BMW 5-Series, Mercedes-Benz E-Class, Jaguar XF, and Infinti M.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S6_and_RS6">S6 and RS6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: S6 and RS6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6#C5" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a> was a high-powered variant of the A6, featuring a modified version of the 4.2-litre <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8 engine</a> producing 250 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (340 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 335 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>) and 420 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (310 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>). It was available as a saloon and Avant although the Avant version was the only one sold in North America.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_RS6" title="Audi RS6">Audi RS6</a></div>
<p>In the late years of the A6 C5 design, an ultra-high-performance limited-run <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_RS6#C5" title="Audi RS6">Audi RS6</a> model was presented. Weighing in excess of 1,840 <a href="/wiki/Kilogram" title="Kilogram">kilograms</a> (4,057 <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">lb</a>) and producing 331 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (450 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 444 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>) and 560 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (413 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>), the RS6 was capable of 0-100 kilometres per hour (62.1 mph) in 4.5 seconds, and on to 200 km/h (124.3 mph) in under 17 seconds. Initially available as only an Avant, a saloon variant was later added; the saloon version being the only version available to the North American market. The RS6 saloon finished first in a May 2003 <i><a href="/wiki/Car_and_Driver" title="Car and Driver">Car and Driver</a></i> comparison test against the BMW M5 (E39), Mercedes-Benz E55 AMG (W210), and Jaguar S-Type R.<i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></i></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="allroad_quattro_.281999.E2.80.932005.29">allroad quattro (1999–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: allroad quattro (1999–2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_(C5,_Facelift)_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_3._Juli_2011,_Essen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="2440" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg/220px-Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg/330px-Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg/440px-Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_%28C5%2C_Facelift%29_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht%2C_3._Juli_2011%2C_Essen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_allroad_quattro_2.5_TDI_(C5,_Facelift)_%E2%80%93_Frontansicht,_3._Juli_2011,_Essen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi allroad quattro 2.5 TDI (Germany)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005_Audi_allroad_(4B_MY04)_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_(2015-07-09)_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/220px-2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/330px-2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/440px-2005_Audi_allroad_%284B_MY04%29_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005_Audi_allroad_(4B_MY04)_2.5_TDI_quattro_Avant_station_wagon_(2015-07-09)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi allroad quattro 2.5 TDI (Australia)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi's C5 series A6 Avant formed the basis for an semi-offroad model in 1999, labeled "Audi allroad quattro". Compared to the regular A6, the allroad featured an advanced <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(vehicle)" title="Suspension (vehicle)">air suspension</a> system, allowing for increased ground clearance; larger wheels with all-terrain tyres, and flared and unpainted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bumper_(automobile)" title="Bumper (automobile)">bumpers</a>, giving it a distinct appearance and more overall flexibility over varying terrain. As the name "allroad quattro" suggests, Audi's <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quattro_(four_wheel_drive_system)" title="Quattro (four wheel drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> system was standard equipment for all versions.</p>
<p>The standard adjustable air suspension system can lift the car high enough to provide 208 mm (8 in) of ground clearance; a low-range mode (an option with manual transmission), absent from other quattro-equipped vehicles, can be selected with the touch of a button. When used together, the two systems made it possible for the allroad to complete an official <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> test-course, thus far it is the only car-based SUV that has been proven capable of doing so in testing. Conversely, the air suspension can lower the vehicle down to only 142 mm (6 in) above road level, and simultaneously stiffen the spring and damper rates to provide a sporty driving experience, much like that of the conventional A6 with the sports suspension.</p>
<p>Audi's 2.7-litre, <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">twin-turbo</a> <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engine</a> with 250 PS (184 kW; 247 hp) of power and 350 N·m (258 lb·ft) of peak torque was available initially, alongside the 2.5-litre TDI diesel unit with 132 kW (177 hp) and 370 N·m (273 lb·ft) of torque. A variant of the corporate 4.2-litre V8 petrol engine, was made available in 2003, and a less powerful TDI (163 bhp) followed in 2004.</p>
<p>Audi stopped production of the allroad in July 2005. Although the model continued to be available for sale throughout 2006 in Europe, there was no 2006 model year for North America.</p>
<p>With the return of the "allroad" nameplate to North America, with the 2013 A4 allroad quattro, the C5-Platform allroad quattro has begun to take the name "Ur-allroad." The '<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ur-" title="wikt:ur-">Ur-</a>' is used in the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German language</a>, as a <a href="/wiki/Affix" title="Affix">prefix</a> to signify 'ancient' or 'early ancestor' (e.g., great-grandmother is Urgroßmutter), and is used informally by car enthusiasts worldwide to refer to the <i>original</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carautoportal-ur_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-carautoportal-ur-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Audi Quattro</a> that was produced from 1980 – 1991 (the "Ur-Quattro"). The use of the term was then extended to the original S4 and S6 models to differentiate them from later models with the same name; and more recently to the C5 allroad models("Ur-allroad"). The need for differentiating the models is likely because the new B8 A4 allroad lacks the C5's adjustable height/load leveling suspension with shock rate adjustment to load and reinforced uni-body, sports only a nominal towing capacity, and lacks a non-allroad A4 wagon counterpart. Some feel that for these reasons it does not live up to the allroad nameplate and is nothing more than an A4 wagon with a trim package.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="C5_engines">C5 engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: C5 engines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_release">Initial release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Initial release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b><i>Typ</i> 4F</b> A6 was released in 2004. Designed by Satoshi Wada in 2001, this model is visually an evolution of the C5, but was lengthened to 4,927 millimetres (194.0 in), and has the new Audi "single-frame grille". Like other contemporary Audis, the A6 has a "tornado line" that runs from the front lights to the rear lights just below the body shoulders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The C6 iteration of the A6 features more sophisticated technology. Most notable is the <a href="/wiki/Multi_Media_Interface" title="Multi Media Interface">Multi Media Interface</a> (MMI), which is a system controlling in-car entertainment, satellite navigation, climate control, car settings such as <a href="/wiki/Height_adjustable_suspension" title="Height adjustable suspension">suspension configuration</a> and optional electronic accessories through a central screen interface. This has the advantage of minimising the wealth of buttons normally found on a dashboard by replacing them with controls which operate multiple devices using the integrated display.</p>
<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engines</a>, the new <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> (FSI) direct injection technology was introduced. Although the line of engines represents the same progression as the former model, all engines were new. The <a href="/wiki/Multitronic" title="Multitronic">multitronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Continuously_variable_transmission" title="Continuously variable transmission">continuously variable transmission</a> continues as an alternative for <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a> models, alongside a new six-speed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiptronic" title="Tiptronic">tiptronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a> available in the <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> models. Audi's "trademark" <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">quattro</a> permanent four-wheel drive is available in most of the lineup, and standard in the most powerful models. quattro is <i>not</i> available on the multitronic variants of the A6, but is available on the manual and tiptronic gear systems. Conversely the tiptronic system is not available on the front-wheel drive variants of the car. The six-speed manual gearbox is available with the 3.2-litre <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6 engine</a>, but not for the North American market.</p>
<p>The Avant was previewd by the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Avantissimo" title="Audi Avantissimo">Audi Avantissimo</a> concept in 2001 and arrived during the course of 2005. The A6 allroad quattro made its debut in 2006, and as before, is an off-road ready version of the Avant, available with either a 2.7-litre V6 or 3.0-litre V6 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">Turbocharged Direct Injection</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a>, or a 3.2-litre V6 or 4.2-litre V8 <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engine</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6L_.282005.E2.80.93.29">A6L (2005–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: A6L (2005–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This is a long <a href="/wiki/Wheelbase" title="Wheelbase">wheelbase</a> version of the A6 sedan for the Chinese market. The vehicle was unveiled in 2005 at the Shanghai Motor Show.</p>
<p>The vehicles went on sale in the middle of 2005. Early models include A6L 2.4, with A6L 2.0 TFSI (170PS) followed shortly after. A6L 3.0 quattro (218PS) and A6L 4.2 quattro (335PS) were introduced in 2005. Other models include A6 3.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S6_2">S6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: S6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6#C6" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a> performance variant was introduced in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">Frankfurt Motor Show</a>, and produced from early 2006 until 2011. It is powered by a 5.2-litre <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> (FSI) <a href="/wiki/V10_engine" title="V10 engine">V10 engine</a> producing a 320 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (435 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 429 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>) and 540 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (398 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>). The S6 reaches 100 kilometres per hour (62.1 mph) from a standstill in 5.2 seconds, and the quarter mile 13.5 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6_allroad_quattro_.282006.E2.80.932011.29">A6 allroad quattro (2006–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: A6 allroad quattro (2006–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_3.0_TFSI_(C6,_Facelift)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_13._M%C3%A4rz_2011,_W%C3%BClfrath.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Facelift A6 allroad quattro 3.0 TFSI</div>

</div>
<p>Audi announced the C6 series allroad in the spring of 2005 and released it in the summer of 2006. This model was called the <b>Audi A6 allroad quattro</b> (unlike the previous version, which was merely called <i>Audi allroad quattro</i>, with no reference to the A6 nomenclature).</p>
<p>The Audi A6 allroad quattro again featured adaptive air suspension and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quattro_(four_wheel_drive_system)" title="Quattro (four wheel drive system)">quattro</a> permanent <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> system. The A6 allroad was powered by a choice of two <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> (FSI) <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engines</a>, a 3.2-litre V6 and a 4.2-litre V8, and two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">TDI</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a>, a 180 PS (132 kW) 2.7 L and a 233 PS (171 kW) 3.0 L. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiptronic" title="Tiptronic">tiptronic</a> gearbox is standard on the 4.2 V8 and the 2.7 TDI, but optional on the 3.2 FSI and 3.0 TDI.</p>
<p>The 6-speed tiptronic transmission system converted high-torque engine power into both sporty performance and operating convenience, with crisp, fast gear changes. Advanced electronics respond efficiently to all driver input in both D (Drive) and S (Sport) programmes, helping to prevent unwanted upshifts when cornering. The five-mode air suspension can be raised by up to 60 mm (2.36 in) to provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_clearance" title="Ground clearance">ground clearance</a> of 185 mm (7.28 in) which is better than the older four-mode.</p>
<p>The car featured a number of off-road styling cues including larger bumpers and sills.</p>
<p>In some European markets, this A6 allroad quattro was more expensive than the larger <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">Audi Q7</a>, but air suspension is an expensive option in the Q7. In its native country, Germany, it cost a few hundred Euros less than the Q7.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, the A6 won the <i><a href="/wiki/World_Car_of_the_Year" title="World Car of the Year">World Car of the Year</a></i> award, and has also won the <i>Practical Caravan</i> "Towcar of the Year" awards, due to its array of towing features such as adjustable suspension height and damping, and the presence of a 123 <a href="/wiki/Towing#Trailer_Stability_Program_or_TSP" title="Towing">Trailer Stability Programme</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="C6_facelift">C6 facelift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: C6 facelift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">

</div>

<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Avant (facelift)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi unveiled a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Facelift_(automobile)" title="Facelift (automobile)">facelifted</a> "C6" Audi A6 on 12 August 2008, at the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Automobile_Salon" title="Moscow International Automobile Salon">Moscow International Motor Show</a>. The refresh incorporates some modern Audi design cues to keep the A6 current with the rest of the Audi lineup.</p>
<p>There are minor cosmetic changes to the front and rear lights which now have daytime running <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LEDs</a>, the taillights extend towards the center of the trunk lid and pinch off at the license plate mount, however their shape remains rectangular compared to the more sculpted light clusters found in the 2008 Audi A5, 2008 Audi A4, and 2009 Audi Q5 (the latter three being all-new generations).</p>
<p>The intakes below the headlamps are inspired by the Audi RS5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The A6's six (per side) front light-emitting diode (LED) daytime running lights (DRLs) are located within the main headlamp housing, similar to RS6's placement of the LEDs (ten per side), whereas on the S6 these front LEDs (five per side) are found adjacent to the fog lamps in the lower front bumper.</p>
<p>The new front and rear fascias from RS6 would be used on the facelifted A6 and S6 lineup.</p>
<p>Also updated for 2009 is the Quattro all-wheel drive setup, which is already found on the 2008 Audi A5 and 2008 Audi A4. This new system features a 40/60 front-to-rear torque split and offers a more balanced feel, reducing the understeer that comes from 50/50 AWD platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are now six petrol and four diesel engines available for the upgraded A6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> All <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">petrol engines</a> now feature cylinder-direct <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> (FSI) technology, and all <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a> now feature <a href="/wiki/Common_rail" title="Common rail">common rail</a> (CR) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">Turbocharged Direct Injection</a> (TDI) technologies. There is a new petrol <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">engine</a>, a 300 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a> (221 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kW</a>; 296 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>) 3.0-litre supercharged V6, badged as 3.0 TFSI or 3.0T. This new engine is shared with the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4" title="Audi S4">Audi S4</a> and S5 Cabriolet, although in the latter two applications in a higher state of tune and mated to a 7-speed S-tronic dual-clutch transmission.</p>
<p>The new engine and revised quattro system give the 2009 Audi A6 3.0 TFSI almost equivalent performance to the Audi S6 5.2 FSI (which is unchanged except for receiving the cosmetic tweaks like the rest of the Audi A6 lineup). Moreover, the S6's weight is 4,500 pounds and 59 percent of weight is distributed to the front which increases understeer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>US models went on sale as 2009 model year vehicles, and arrived in U.S. dealerships by the beginning of January. Early models include A6 3.2 FSI (sedan), A6 3.0 TFSI quattro (sedan/Avant), A6 4.2 FSI quattro (sedan), S6 5.2 FSI (sedan).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RS6_.282008.E2.80.93.29">RS6 (2008–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: RS6 (2008–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_RS6" title="Audi RS6">Audi RS6</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_(9)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2030" data-file-width="3983" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/400px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%289%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_(4)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1730" data-file-width="2827" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/400px-Audi_RS6_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%284%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">RS6 sedan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The latest version of ultra-high-performance <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_RS6#C6" title="Audi RS6">Audi RS6</a> was launched in September 2008 and produced until the third quarter of 2010. Based upon the V10 engine powering the S6, the RS6 features an all-<a href="/wiki/Aluminium_alloy" title="Aluminium alloy">aluminium alloy</a> 4,991 <a href="/wiki/Cubic_centimetre" title="Cubic centimetre">cc</a> (304.6 <a href="/wiki/Cubic_inch" title="Cubic inch">cu in</a>) <a href="/wiki/V10_engine" title="V10 engine">V10</a> <a href="/wiki/Twin-turbo" title="Twin-turbo">twin-turbocharged</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> engine with a <a href="/wiki/Dry_sump" title="Dry sump">dry sump</a> lubrication system. It produces a power output of 426 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">kilowatts</a> (579 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">PS</a>; 571 <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">bhp</a>), and 650 <a href="/wiki/Newton_metre" title="Newton metre">newton metres</a> (479 <a href="/wiki/Pound-foot_(torque)" title="Pound-foot (torque)">lbf·ft</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">torque</a>, making it the most powerful vehicle ever produced by Audi at the time. This has now been surpassed by the Audi R8.</p>
<p>Initially available only as an Avant, the saloon version went on sale in mid-October 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6L">A6L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: A6L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="577" data-file-width="1300" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg/220px-Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg/330px-Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg/440px-Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A6L_C6_facelift_China_2012-04-22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi A6 L (China)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The A6L is a longer wheelbase version of the A6 sedan for the Chinese market. The vehicle was unveiled at Auto Shanghai 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Early models included the 2.7 TDI powerplant (189PS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_release_2">Initial release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Initial release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fourth generation C7 series Audi A6 (internally designated <i><b>Typ 4G</b></i>) was launched in early 2011 for the European market and in other markets soon after. It is heavily influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a> (D4), pulling elements from its exterior details.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The A6 shares its interior, platform, and powertrain (<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group_MLB_platform" title="Volkswagen Group MLB platform">Modular Longitudinal Platform</a>) with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A7" title="Audi A7">Audi A7</a> four door sedan, which had been released shortly before also in 2011. Compared to the A8 and A7, the A6 has the most aggressive front fascia and LED headlights (optional full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LED_headlamp" title="LED headlamp">LED headlamps</a>). Design work began in 2006, with Jurgen Loffler's exterior design being chosen in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new A6 increased its wheelbase by nearly 3 inches (76 mm) and its width by 2.7 inches (69 mm). The redesign also decreased the car's <a href="/wiki/Automobile_drag_coefficient" title="Automobile drag coefficient">drag coefficient</a> to 0.25 Cd.</p>
<p>European engine choices for the C7 include two petrol engines – a 2.8-litre FSI V6 with 204 horsepower (152 kW) and a 300 horsepower (224 kW), 3.0-litre supercharged FSI engine – and three diesel engines – a 2.0-litre inline four-cylinder and a 3.0-litre turbocharged diesel engine in three states of tune.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A6future_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-A6future-37">[37]</a></sup> The European A6 3.0 TFSI will have optional a seven-speed dual-clutch transmission and an air suspension, two features that will not be available on the United States model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>For North America, the Audi A6 3.0 TFSI quattro will be powered by a 3.0-litre supercharged V6 putting out 310 PS (228 kW; 306 hp) 325 lb·ft (441 N·m), the same engine carried over from the previous-generation A6 3.0 TFSI, but in a higher state of tune and mated to an eight-speed automatic transmission. For the United States but not the Canadian market, there will be an entry-level Audi A6 2.0 TFSI <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=FrontTrak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="FrontTrak (page does not exist)">FrontTrak</a> (front-wheel drive) with a 2.0-litre turbocharged inline-four, the same engine in the Audi A4 and Q5, but mated to the Multitronic CVT (continuous variable transmission).</p>
<p>The 2012 model year A6 features all the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_driver_assistance_systems" title="Advanced driver assistance systems">driver assistance systems</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">A8</a>, plus it adds <a href="/wiki/Automotive_head-up_display" title="Automotive head-up display">automotive head-up display</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_lane_assist" title="Active lane assist">active lane assist</a>. Full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LED_headlamp" title="LED headlamp">LED headlamps</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_high_beam" title="Automatic high beam">Automatic high beam</a> switching or Audi <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptive_light" title="Adaptive light">adaptive light</a> (<a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">Xenon</a>) with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variable_headlight_range_control" title="Variable headlight range control">variable headlight range control</a>.</p>

<p>Audi unveiled the 2015 C7 mid-life facelift at the 2014 Paris Motor Show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The refresh includes styling tweaks to the car's exterior, engine line-up, transmission and <a href="/wiki/Multi_Media_Interface" title="Multi Media Interface">MMI</a> infotainment system with faster <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tegra_3" title="Tegra 3">Tegra 3</a> processor, <a href="/wiki/Handwriting_recognition" title="Handwriting recognition">Handwriting recognition</a>, <b>Audi connect</b> <a href="/wiki/Telematics" title="Telematics">Telematics</a> with <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_art" title="State of the art">state of the art</a> <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_internet" title="Mobile internet">mobile internet</a> (and online updates for the navigation map), and advanced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrix_LED" title="Matrix LED">Matrix LED</a> headlights.</p>
<p>All three TFSI and five TDI engines now meet the Euro 6 emission standard. The new TDI Ultra model now comes with glass fiber-reinforced polymer (GFRP) springs and both ultra models now come with S-tronic (dual clutch) transmission.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6_hybrid_.282012.E2.80.93.29">A6 hybrid (2012–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: A6 hybrid (2012–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A6_hybrid_(C7)_front.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2508" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG/220px-Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG/330px-Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG/440px-Audi_A6_hybrid_%28C7%29_front.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A6_hybrid_(C7)_front.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A6 Hybrid</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle_drivetrain#Full_Hybrids" title="Hybrid vehicle drivetrain">hybrid electric</a> variant was also available for the first time in the A6, offering a 2-litre TFSI 211 metric horsepower (155 kW) engine combined with a 45 PS (33 kW) electric motor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A6future_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-A6future-37">[37]</a></sup> Electric power is supplied via 1.3kWh lithium-ion battery, with electric-only range of 3 km for constant 60 km/h (37.28 mph) drive and top speed of 100 km/h (62.14 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-green.autoblog.com_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-green.autoblog.com-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The market launch of the A6 Hybrid was scheduled for 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, production of the US model was delayed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6_allroad_quattro_.282012.E2.80.93present.29">A6 allroad quattro (2012–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: A6 allroad quattro (2012–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2400" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG/200px-2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG/300px-2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG/400px-2015_Punta_del_Este_ePrix_-_Audi_A6_allroad_quattro_Audi_Sport_Abt.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg/200px-Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg/300px-Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg/400px-Audi_-_A6_-_Mondial_de_l%27Automobile_de_Paris_2012_-_203.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A6 allroad quattro</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2013 <b>A6 allroad quattro</b> was launched at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">Geneva Motor Show</a>, along with the 2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_RS4" title="Audi RS4">RS4 Avant</a>. Sales began in 2012. The first UK deliveries arrived in July 2012.</p>
<p>The allroad model contains several unique features. Audi designed more than 1,100 new, unique parts for the allroad, setting it apart from the standard A6 and making it a true all-terrain vehicle. Most obvious, the allroad received special bumpers and fender flares, giving it an aggressive offroad appearance. The bumpers and fender flares feature a tough-wearing, matte finish, contrasting the rest of the body. The roof received this same coating, as well as four longitudinal ribs for increased strength. The unique bumpers also have integrated aluminum skid plates. The allroad featured larger diameter tires than the standard A6 for improved offroad capabilities. Redesigned headlights, larger side mirrors, and a lack of door "rub strips" are unique to the allroad.</p>
<p>The allroad comes standard with an <a href="/wiki/Height_adjustable_suspension" title="Height adjustable suspension">adjustable</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_suspension" title="Air suspension">air suspension</a> system can lift the car high enough to provide 208 mm (8 in) of ground clearance; a low-range mode (an option with manual transmission), absent from other quattro-equipped vehicles, can be selected with the touch of a button. When used together, the two systems made it possible for the allroad to complete an official <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> test-course, thus far it is the only car-based SUV that has been proven capable of doing so in testing.</p>
<p>Conversely, the air suspension can lower the vehicle down to only 142 mm (6 in) above road level, and simultaneously stiffen the spring and damper rates to provide a sporty driving experience, much like that of the conventional A6 with the sports suspension.</p>
<p>German model went on sale in spring 2012. Early models included 3.0 TFSI quattro (310PS), 3.0 TDI quattro (204PS), 3.0 TDI quattro (245PS), 3.0 TDI quattro (313PS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A6_L_.282012.E2.80.93.29">A6 L (2012–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: A6 L (2012–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The A6 L (built in China for the Chinese market as a long wheelbase alternative to the standard A6) was unveiled in 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_International_Sports_Arena" title="Guangzhou International Sports Arena">Guangzhou International Sports Arena</a>. Early models include A6 L TFSI, A6 L 30 FSI, A6 L 35 FSI, A6 L 35 FSI quattro, A6 L 50 TFSI quattro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>

<td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S6_.282012.E2.80.93.29">S6 (2012–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A6&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: S6 (2012–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Available in S6 sedan and S6 Avant, they included twin-turbo V8 engine rated 420 PS (309 kW; 414 hp)@5500–6400rpm and 550 N·m (406 lbf·ft)@1450–5250rpm, recuperation and start-stop systems, cylinder deactivation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_Noise_Cancellation" title="Active Noise Cancellation">Active Noise Cancellation</a> system, seven-speed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S_tronic" title="S tronic">S tronic</a> transmission, quattro permanent all-wheel drive system with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-locking_center_differential" title="Self-locking center differential">self-locking center differential</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torque_vectoring" title="Torque vectoring">torque vectoring</a> (optional sport differential), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptive_air_suspension" title="Adaptive air suspension">adaptive air suspension</a> lowers the body by 10 mm (0 in), internally ventilated brake discs (optional carbon fiber-ceramic discs), matt black calipers with S6 logos, 8.5Jx19-inch cast aluminum wheels in a unique five parallel-spoke design (optional seven different 19- or 20-inch wheels (four from quattro GmbH), including 20-inch titanium-look wheels with a five-arm rotor design), 255/40-series tires, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_drive_select&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Audi drive select (page does not exist)">Audi drive select</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Driving_dynamics_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Driving dynamics system (page does not exist)">driving dynamics system</a>, optional <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dynamic_steering&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dynamic steering (page does not exist)">dynamic steering</a>, single-frame grille with aluminum applications and chromed horizontal double bars, exterior mirrors feature aluminum-look housings, S6 sedan with spoiler on the trunk (S6 Avant has a roof spoiler), diffuser on the rear bumper in platinum gray with an aluminum-look offset edge, four elliptical chrome-tipped tailpipes, choice of eight body colors (including exclusive shades Estoril Blue, crystal effect and Prism Silver, crystal effect), body decorated with S6 and V8T badges, leather sport steering wheel with colored stitching, footrest and pedals and soft keys of the MMI operating system in an aluminum-look finish, decorative inlays in matt brushed aluminum (optional carbon, fine grain ash natural brown, layered Beaufort oak), choice of 3 colours for headlining, instrument panel, carpet and seats (black, lunar silver and goa beige (only for the seat upholstery)); Pearl Nappa leather and Alcantara seat upholstery (optional Milano and Valcona leather), height-adjustable sport seats with power lumbar supports and embossed S logos (optional power-adjustable comfort seats with memory function, power-adjustable S sport seats with integrated head restraints).</p>
<p>Other options include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xenon_plus" title="Xenon plus">xenon plus</a> headlights with an all-weather light, LED rear lights, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromechanical_parking_brake" title="Electromechanical parking brake">electromechanical parking brake</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Driver_information_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Driver information system (page does not exist)">driver information system</a> with color display, MMI radio plus includes a <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a> interface, Audi sound system with ten speakers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MMI_navigation" title="MMI navigation">MMI navigation</a> plus (hard drive, an eight-inch monitor, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MMI_touch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MMI touch (page does not exist)">MMI touch</a> input system), 15-speaker <a href="/wiki/Bang_%26_Olufsen" title="Bang &amp; Olufsen">Bang &amp; Olufsen</a> Advanced Sound System.</p>
<p>The S6 sedan was unveiled in the 2011 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Motor_Show" title="Frankfurt Motor Show">Frankfurt Motor Show</a>.</p>
<p>S6 sedan and Avant models went on sale in spring 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
